The critical operation is at line 163:\\n```\\nbucket.Put(key, value)\\n```\\n\\nThis stores the key-value pair in the BoltDB transaction, which initially lives only in memory.\\n\\nFinally, the in-memory transaction must be committed to disk. The `batchTx.commit()` function (lines 261-288) executes this commit. The key operation is at line 271:\\n```\\nerr := t.tx.Commit()\\n```\\n\\nThis commits the BoltDB transaction to the persistent disk storage, ensuring the Deployment data is durably stored even if the etcd process crashes. The critical operation is at line 163:\\n```\\nbucket.Put(key, value)\\n```\\n\\nThis stores the key-value pair in the BoltDB transaction, which initially lives only in memory.\\n\\nFinally, the in-memory transaction must be committed to disk. The `batchTx.commit()` function (lines 261-288) executes this commit. The key operation is at line 271:\\n```\\nerr := t.tx.Commit()\\n```\\n\\nThis commits the BoltDB transaction to the persistent disk storage, ensuring the Deployment data is durably stored even if the etcd process crashes. This prevents invalid Deployments from being stored.\\n\\n3. **Admission control**: Runs the validating and mutating admission controllers to ensure the object passes cluster-level policies.\\n\\n4. **Storage delegation**: Calls `e.Storage.Create()` to write the validated Deployment to the backend storage.\\n\\n### 3. Storage Layer (etcd-io/etcd)\\n\\nOnce the API server has validated the Deployment, it delegates persistence to the etcd backend. The etcd storage layer implements a hierarchical write pipeline that efficiently batches writes to disk.\\n\\nThe write flow begins at the KV store interface in `etcd-io/etcd/server/mvcc/kv_view.go`. The `writeView.Put()` function (lines 52-56) is the high-level entry point for storing key-value pairs. It accepts the Deployment's key (typically `/kubernetes.io/deployments/namespace/name`) and serialized value.\\n\\nNext, the write request enters a transaction context in `etcd-io/etcd/server/mvcc/kvstore_txn.go`. The `storeTxnWrite.put()` method (lines 190-253) marshals the Deployment data into an etcd KeyValue protobuf message and stages it for backend persistence. At line 226, it calls:\\n```\\ntw.tx.UnsafeSeqPut(buckets.Key, ibytes, d)\\n```\\n\\nThis delegates to the backend batch transaction layer in `etcd-io/etcd/server/mvcc/backend/batch_tx.go`. The `batchTx.unsafePut()` function (lines 149-171) writes the staged data to the in-memory BoltDB transaction buffer. The critical operation is at line 163:\\n```\\nbucket.Put(key, value)\\n```\\n\\nThis stores the key-value pair in the BoltDB transaction, which initially lives only in memory.\\n\\nFinally, the in-memory transaction must be committed to disk. The `batchTx.commit()` function (lines 261-288) executes this commit. The key operation is at line 271:\\n```\\nerr := t.tx.Commit()\\n```\\n\\nThis commits the BoltDB transaction to the persistent disk storage, ensuring the Deployment data is durably stored even if the etcd process crashes. The commit is triggered either explicitly via `ForceCommit()` or automatically every 100 milliseconds by the backend's background commit loop.\\n\\n### Summary\\n\\nThe complete flow traces from the client library's HTTP construction, through the API server's validation and admission pipeline, to etcd's transactional write-and-commit architecture:\\n\\n- **Client**: Serializes Deployment → HTTP POST\\n- **API Server**: Deserializes → Validates → Admits → Delegates to storage\\n- **etcd**: Stages write in transaction → Buffers in memory → Commits to disk\\n\\nThis three-layer architecture ensures that client requests are validated at every stage before being permanently stored in the distributed key-value store.\"\n}\n","numLines":60,"startLine":1,"totalLines":60}}}
